## GHSA-f75j-4cw6-rmx4 · code.gitea.io/gitea

2026-07-21 · Go · **CRITICAL** 9.8 · Pattern: `RACE_CONDITION→DOUBLE_SPEND`

### Root cause

The Gitea Docker image, when configured with `REVERSE_PROXY_TRUSTED_PROXIES = *`, allowed any source IP to impersonate any user via the `X-WEBAUTH-USER` header. Additionally, the TOTP (Time-based One-Time Password) validation logic was susceptible to replay attacks because it did not atomically consume the passcode after successful validation, allowing the same passcode to be used multiple times within its validity window.

### Impact

An attacker could bypass two-factor authentication by replaying a valid TOTP passcode. In the context of the Docker image misconfiguration, this could be combined with user impersonation to gain unauthorized access to user accounts.

### Key diff

```
--- a/models/auth/twofactor.go
+++ b/models/auth/twofactor.go
-func (t *TwoFactor) ValidateTOTP(passcode string) (bool, error) {
+func (t *TwoFactor) ValidateAndConsumeTOTP(ctx context.Context, passcode string) (bool, error) {
 	return totp.Validate(passcode, secretStr), nil
 }
+	// Conditional update: only a row whose stored passcode differs from this one is updated, so a
+	// replay (or a concurrent duplicate) matches zero rows and is rejected. The row lock taken by
+	// the UPDATE serializes racing requests, closing the read-validate-write TOCTOU window.
+	t.LastUsedPasscode = passcode
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces `ValidateAndConsumeTOTP` which atomically validates and consumes a TOTP passcode by updating a `last_used_passcode` field in the database. This prevents replay attacks by ensuring a passcode can only be used once. The web and API authentication flows are updated to use this new atomic validation function.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 2 occurrences**
> Languages: PHP, Go
> → GHSA-9rh9-hf3w-9fgg

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/go-gitea/gitea/commit/99f8b3d9a1d32f4c39828e07971455a18191e0b9)

## GHSA-hg5r-vq93-9fv6 · code.gitea.io/gitea

2026-07-21 · Go · **CRITICAL** 9.6 · Pattern: `WEAK_CRYPTO→HASH`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an ambiguity in how HMAC signatures were generated for Gitea Actions artifacts. The previous implementation concatenated string and integer values directly into the HMAC function without length-prefixing or clear delimiters. This allowed an attacker to craft inputs where different combinations of values (e.g., artifactName and taskID) could produce the same HMAC signature, leading to a collision.

### Impact

An attacker could exploit this ambiguity to read artifacts from other repositories (cross-repository artifact read) or manipulate the upload state of artifacts in other tasks (cross-task upload-state write), bypassing intended access controls.

### Key diff

```
--- a/routers/api/actions/artifactsv4.go
+++ b/routers/api/actions/artifactsv4.go
@@ -161,13 +161,7 @@ func ArtifactsV4Routes(prefix string) *web.Router {
 }
 
 func (r *artifactV4Routes) buildSignature(endpoint, expires, artifactName string, taskID, artifactID int64) []byte {
-	mac := hmac.New(sha256.New, setting.GetGeneralTokenSigningSecret())
-	mac.Write([]byte(endpoint))
-	mac.Write([]byte(expires))
-	mac.Write([]byte(artifactName))
-	_, _ = fmt.Fprint(mac, taskID)
-	_, _ = fmt.Fprint(mac, artifactID)
-	return mac.Sum(nil)
+	return actions.BuildSignature("v4", endpoint, expires, artifactName, strconv.FormatInt(taskID, 10), strconv.FormatInt(artifactID, 10))
 }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new `BuildSignature` helper function that explicitly length-prefixes all input values before feeding them into the HMAC algorithm. It also adds a 'tag' parameter to distinguish signatures for different purposes. This ensures that each component of the signed data is unambiguously separated, preventing collision attacks.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 3 occurrences**
> Languages: RUST, JavaScript, Go
> → GHSA-3g92-f9ch-qjcm
> → GHSA-39pv-4j6c-2g6v

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/go-gitea/gitea/commit/1c2d5e9b03f71dd12d450b2af9a79f2557b50226)

## GHSA-pf56-329r-95rw · @sigstore/oci

2026-07-21 · JavaScript · **CRITICAL** 9.6 · Pattern: `CREDENTIAL_LEAK→LOG_EXPOSURE`

### Root cause

The vulnerability stemmed from an overly broad credential matching logic. The system used `key.includes(registry)` to find credentials, which meant that credentials for a registry like `myregistry.com` could be inadvertently sent to an attacker-controlled registry like `evilmyregistry.com` because the latter's name included the former.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious registry name that is a substring of a legitimate registry for which the user has credentials. When the user attempts to interact with the attacker's registry, their legitimate credentials for the intended registry would be leaked to the attacker.

### Key diff

```
-	    Object.keys(dockerConfig.auths || {}).find((key) =>
-	      key.includes(registry)
-	    ) || registry;
+	  const target = canonicalizeRegistry(registry);
+	  const credKey = Object.keys(dockerConfig.auths || {}).find(
+	    (key) => canonicalizeRegistry(key) === target
+	  );
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a `canonicalizeRegistry` function to normalize registry hostnames, including handling Docker Hub aliases. It then changes the credential lookup to use an exact match (`canonicalizeRegistry(key) === target`) instead of a substring match, ensuring credentials are only sent to the exact intended registry.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 6 occurrences**
> Languages: Java, Go, Python, C#, JavaScript
> → GHSA-cmxv-58fp-fm3g
> → GHSA-pm7q-rjjx-979p
> → GHSA-f7j3-774f-rfhj
> → GHSA-vh4v-2xq2-g5cg
> → GHSA-q62h-354g-5r85

🔗 [View commit](https://github.com/sigstore/sigstore-js/commit/85c58380758b97ce1b74ef470e55cc21f9d3aa89)

## GHSA-p63j-vcc4-9vmv · @vitest/browser

2026-07-21 · JavaScript · **CRITICAL** 9.4 · Pattern: `PATH_TRAVERSAL→FILE_WRITE`

### Root cause

The Vitest browser mode allowed certain commands (like screenshotMatcher and file system operations) to bypass file access permission gates. Specifically, the `assertFileAccess` and `assertWrite` checks were not consistently applied or were missing in critical code paths, allowing an attacker to read from or write to arbitrary files outside the intended project root.

### Impact

An attacker could read or write arbitrary files on the server running Vitest, potentially leading to remote code execution, sensitive data disclosure, or denial of service.

### Key diff

```
--- a/packages/browser/src/node/commands/screenshotMatcher/index.ts
+++ b/packages/browser/src/node/commands/screenshotMatcher/index.ts
@@ -555,8 +560,10 @@ async function takeScreenshotData({
 }
 
 /** Writes encoded images to disk, creating parent directories as needed. */
-async function writeScreenshot(path: string, image: TypedArray) {
+async function writeScreenshot(path: string, image: TypedArray, project: TestProject) {
   try {
+    assertBrowserApiWrite(project, path)
+    assertBrowserFileAccess(project, path)
     await mkdir(dirname(path), { recursive: true })
     await writeFile(path, image)
   }
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces new utility functions `assertBrowserApiWrite` and `assertBrowserFileAccess` to centralize and enforce file access and write permissions. These checks are now consistently applied to all relevant browser commands, including screenshot matching and direct file system operations, ensuring that file paths are confined to the project root and write operations respect configuration settings.

## GHSA-7wvc-rvp7-w99x · code.gitea.io/gitea

2026-07-21 · Go · **HIGH** 7.7 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTH→ENDPOINT`

### Root cause

The `getAccessMode` function previously panicked on unknown SSH sub-verbs for LFS, but in production, it would return `perm.AccessModeNone`. This `AccessModeNone` was then incorrectly interpreted as a valid, albeit minimal, access mode, allowing the request to proceed without proper authorization checks for private repositories.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malformed SSH LFS sub-verb to bypass authentication and gain unauthorized read access to private repositories.

### Key diff

```
--- a/cmd/serv.go
+++ b/cmd/serv.go
@@ -113,23 +113,25 @@ func handleCliResponseExtra(extra private.ResponseExtra) error {
 	return nil
 }
 
-func getAccessMode(verb, lfsVerb string) perm.AccessMode {
+func getAccessMode(verb, lfsVerb string) (mode perm.AccessMode, ok bool) {
 	switch verb {
 	case git.CmdVerbUploadPack, git.CmdVerbUploadArchive:
-		return perm.AccessModeRead
+		return perm.AccessModeRead, true
 	case git.CmdVerbReceivePack:
-		return perm.AccessModeWrite
+		return perm.AccessModeWrite, true
 	case git.CmdVerbLfsAuthenticate, git.CmdVerbLfsTransfer:
 		switch lfsVerb {
 		case git.CmdSubVerbLfsUpload:
-			return perm.AccessModeWrite
+			return perm.AccessModeWrite, true
 		case git.CmdSubVerbLfsDownload:
-			return perm.AccessModeRead
+			return perm.AccessModeRead, true
 		}
 	}
-	// should be unreachable
-	setting.PanicInDevOrTesting("unknown verb: %s %s", verb, lfsVerb)
-	return perm.AccessModeNone
+	return perm.AccessModeNone, false
 }
 
 func runServ(ctx context.Context, c *cli.Command) error {
@@ -247,7 +249,10 @@ func runServ(ctx context.Context, c *cli.Command) error {
 		}
 	}
 
-	requestedMode := getAccessMode(verb, lfsVerb)
+	requestedMode, ok := getAccessMode(verb, lfsVerb)
+	if !ok {
+		return fail(ctx, "Unknown git command", "Unknown git command %s %s", verb, lfsVerb)
+	}
 
 	results, extra := private.ServCommand(ctx, keyID, username, reponame, requestedMode, verb, lfsVerb)
```

### Fix summary

The `getAccessMode` function was modified to return a boolean `ok` value indicating whether the verb was recognized. If the verb is not recognized (`ok` is false), the request is now explicitly rejected, preventing the `AccessModeNone` from being misused.

## GHSA-rwj8-pgh3-r573 · gitpython

2026-07-21 · Python · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `INFO_DISCLOSURE→ERROR_MESSAGE`

### Root cause

The `Git.polish_url` method, used when cloning repositories, automatically expanded environment variables and user home directories via `os.path.expandvars()` and `os.path.expanduser()`. This behavior was applied to untrusted URLs provided by users, allowing an attacker to craft a malicious URL that would cause the victim's environment variables to be included in the URL sent to a remote Git server.

### Impact

An attacker could exfiltrate sensitive environment variables (e.g., API keys, credentials, tokens) from the system running the GitPython application by providing a specially crafted repository URL. This information would then be sent to a server controlled by the attacker.

### Key diff

```
--- a/git/repo/base.py
+++ b/git/repo/base.py
@@ -1452,8 +1452,9 @@ def _clone(
         if multi_options:
             multi = shlex.split(" ".join(multi_options))
 
+        clone_url = Git.polish_url(url, expand_vars=False)
         if not allow_unsafe_protocols:
-            Git.check_unsafe_protocols(url)
+            Git.check_unsafe_protocols(clone_url)
         if not allow_unsafe_options:
```

### Fix summary

A new `expand_vars` parameter was added to `Git.polish_url` and related `cygpath` functions, defaulting to `True`. When cloning a repository, `Repo._clone` now explicitly calls `Git.polish_url` with `expand_vars=False` for the untrusted URL, preventing the expansion of environment variables and user directories.

## GHSA-v2hh-gcrm-f6hx · fast-uri

2026-07-21 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 7.5 · Pattern: `SSRF→INTERNAL_ACCESS`

### Root cause

The `fast-uri` library did not correctly handle literal backslashes (U+005C) in the authority component of a URI. While RFC 3986 does not consider backslash a valid URI character, some parsers (like WHATWG URL) might normalize it to a forward slash, leading to a different interpretation of the host compared to Node's native URL parser.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a URI with a literal backslash to bypass host-based allowlists or security checks, potentially leading to Server-Side Request Forgery (SSRF) or open redirect vulnerabilities by causing the application to connect to an unintended host.

### Key diff

```
--- a/index.js
+++ b/index.js
@@ -248,6 +252,19 @@ function parseWithStatus (uri, opts) {
     }
   }
 
+  const authorityMatch = uri.match(AUTHORITY_PREFIX)
+  if (authorityMatch !== null && authorityMatch[1].indexOf('\\') !== -1) {
+    parsed.error = 'URI authority must not contain a literal backslash.'
+    malformedAuthorityOrPort = true
+  }
+
   const matches = uri.match(URI_PARSE)
 
   if (matches) {
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new regular expression `AUTHORITY_PREFIX` to specifically capture the authority component. It then explicitly checks if this component contains a literal backslash. If found, the URI is marked as malformed, preventing its parsing and use, thus avoiding host confusion.

## GHSA-gx3v-q759-g323 · code.gitea.io/gitea

2026-07-21 · Go · **HIGH** 7.1 · Pattern: `RACE_CONDITION→TOCTOU`

### Root cause

The application validated Time-based One-Time Passwords (TOTP) without atomically consuming them, leading to a Time-of-Check to Time-of-Use (TOCTOU) race condition. Additionally, the Basic-Auth X-Gitea-OTP surface lacked a replay check, allowing a valid TOTP passcode to be reused.

### Impact

An attacker could potentially reuse a valid TOTP passcode multiple times, or exploit a race condition to bypass 2FA by submitting the same passcode concurrently, thereby gaining unauthorized access to user accounts.

### Key diff

```
--- a/models/auth/twofactor.go
+++ b/models/auth/twofactor.go
@@ -108,18 +109,41 @@ func (t *TwoFactor) SetSecret(secretString string) error {
 	return nil
 }
 
-// ValidateTOTP validates the provided passcode.
-func (t *TwoFactor) ValidateTOTP(passcode string) (bool, error) {
+// ValidateAndConsumeTOTP validates the passcode and atomically records it as used so that the
+// same passcode cannot be redeemed more than once (RFC 6238 §5.2). It returns false for an
+// invalid passcode as well as for a replay, including the case where a concurrent request with
+// the same passcode won the race first. All TOTP login surfaces must go through this helper.
+func (t *TwoFactor) ValidateAndConsumeTOTP(ctx context.Context, passcode string) (bool, error) {
+	ok, err := t.validateTOTP(passcode)
+	if err != nil || !ok {
+		return false, err
+	}
+	// Conditional update: only a row whose stored passcode differs from this one is updated, so a
+	// replay (or a concurrent duplicate) matches zero rows and is rejected. The row lock taken by
+	// the UPDATE serializes racing requests, closing the read-validate-write TOCTOU window.
+	t.LastUsedPasscode = passcode
+	n, err := db.GetEngine(ctx).ID(t.ID).
+		Where(builder.Or(builder.IsNull{"last_used_passcode"}, builder.Neq{"last_used_passcode": passcode})).
+		Cols("last_used_passcode").Update(t)
+	if err != nil {
+		return false, err
+	}
+	return n == 1, nil
+}
 
--- a/routers/web/auth/2fa.go
+++ b/routers/web/auth/2fa.go
@@ -58,14 +58,14 @@ func TwoFactorPost(ctx *context.Context) {
 		return
 	}
 
-	// Validate the passcode with the stored TOTP secret.
-	ok, err := twofa.ValidateTOTP(form.Passcode)
+	// Validate the passcode and atomically consume it to prevent reuse/replay.
+	ok, err := twofa.ValidateAndConsumeTOTP(ctx, form.Passcode)
 	if err != nil {
 		ctx.ServerError("UserSignIn", err)
 		return
 	}
 
-	if ok && twofa.LastUsedPasscode != form.Passcode {
+	if ok {
 		remember := ctx.Session.Get("twofaRemember").(bool)
 		u, err := user_model.GetUserByID(ctx, id)
 		if err != nil
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new `ValidateAndConsumeTOTP` function that atomically validates and marks a TOTP passcode as used within a single database transaction. This prevents both replay attacks and TOCTOU race conditions by ensuring a passcode can only be successfully redeemed once.

> ⚡ **Pattern match — 11 occurrences**
> Languages: JavaScript, Go, Python, RUST
> → GHSA-gj9q-8w99-mp8j

## GHSA-8r6m-32jq-jx6q · fast-xml-parser

2026-07-21 · JavaScript · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The XML parser did not properly limit the number of entity expansions when multiple DOCTYPE declarations were present in an XML document. Each DOCTYPE declaration would reset the internal entity expansion counters, allowing an attacker to repeatedly define and expand entities, leading to excessive memory consumption and CPU usage.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious XML document that, when parsed, would consume excessive system resources (CPU and memory), leading to a denial of service for the application using the parser.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/xmlparser/OrderedObjParser.js
+++ b/src/xmlparser/OrderedObjParser.js
@@ -378,6 +380,8 @@ const parseXml = function (xmlData) {
         i = endIndex;
       } else if (c1 === 33
         && xmlData.charCodeAt(i + 2) === 68) { //'!D'
+        if (this.doctypefound) throw new Error("Multiple DOCTYPE declarations found.");
+        this.doctypefound = true;
         const result = docTypeReader.readDocType(xmlData, i);
         this.entityDecoder.addInputEntities(result.entities);
         i = result.i;
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new flag, `this.doctypefound`, to track whether a DOCTYPE declaration has already been processed. If a subsequent DOCTYPE declaration is encountered, the parser now throws an error, preventing the entity expansion counters from being reset and mitigating the resource exhaustion vulnerability.

## GHSA-8whx-365g-h9vv · loofah

2026-07-21 · Ruby · **LOW** 0.0 · Pattern: `UNSANITIZED_INPUT→XSS`

### Root cause

The `allowed_uri?` method in Loofah did not correctly handle `javascript:` URIs that were split by HTML5 named whitespace character references (e.g., `&Tab;`, `&NewLine;`). While it unescaped HTML entities and stripped control characters, it missed these specific named character references, allowing an attacker to bypass the URI validation.

### Impact

An attacker could craft a malicious URI using named whitespace character references to bypass Loofah's sanitization, potentially leading to Cross-Site Scripting (XSS) by executing arbitrary JavaScript in the user's browser.

### Key diff

```
--- a/lib/loofah/html5/scrub.rb
+++ b/lib/loofah/html5/scrub.rb
@@ -168,11 +172,15 @@ def scrub_attribute_that_allows_local_ref(attr_node)
         # This method can be used to validate URI attribute values without
         # requiring a Nokogiri DOM node.
         def allowed_uri?(uri_string)
-          # Replace control characters both before and after unescaping.
+          # Control characters are stripped both before and after unescaping, since
+          # unescaping can produce them. That strip must precede
+          # WHITESPACE_CHARACTER_REFERENCES: removing a control character can reveal a
+          # named whitespace reference.
           uri_string = CGI.unescapeHTML(uri_string.gsub(CONTROL_CHARACTERS, ""))
-            .gsub(CONTROL_CHARACTERS, "")
-            .gsub("&colon;", ":")
-            .downcase
+          uri_string.gsub!(CONTROL_CHARACTERS, "")
+          uri_string.gsub!(WHITESPACE_CHARACTER_REFERENCES, "")
+          uri_string.gsub!("&colon;", ":")
+          uri_string.downcase!
           if URI_PROTOCOL_REGEX.match?(uri_string)
             protocol = uri_string.split(SafeList::PROTOCOL_SEPARATOR)[0]
             return false unless SafeList::ALLOWED_PROTOCOLS.include?(protocol)
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a new regular expression `WHITESPACE_CHARACTER_REFERENCES` to explicitly detect and remove HTML5 named whitespace character references like `&Tab;` and `&NewLine;` from URI strings. This ensures that `javascript:` schemes obfuscated with these references are correctly identified and blocked during URI validation.

## GHSA-g9g6-qhrc-p3qc · code.gitea.io/gitea

2026-07-21 · Go · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `MISSING_AUTHZ→RESOURCE`

### Root cause

The system incorrectly assumed that any deactivated user attempting to sign in via OAuth should be reactivated. It failed to distinguish between users deactivated by an administrator and users deactivated automatically due to invalid OAuth tokens. This allowed an attacker to bypass an administrator's explicit deactivation by simply signing in through OAuth.

### Impact

An attacker could reactivate an account that an administrator had intentionally disabled, thereby regaining access to the system and potentially escalating privileges if the account had elevated roles.

### Key diff

```
--- a/routers/web/auth/oauth.go
+++ b/routers/web/auth/oauth.go
@@ -364,9 +364,21 @@ func handleOAuth2SignIn(ctx *context.Context, authSource *auth.Source, u *user_m
 
 	opts := &user_service.UpdateOptions{}
 
-	// Reactivate user if they are deactivated
+	// Reactivate user only if they were disabled by the OAuth2 auto sync cron (invalid_grant),
+	// which clears AccessToken/RefreshToken/ExpiresAt on the ExternalLoginUser row
+	// An admin-disabled user has no such signature, so we leave IsActive alone
+	// and let verifyAuthWithOptions route them through the prohibit-login / activate page.
 	if !u.IsActive {
-		opts.IsActive = optional.Some(true)
+		extLogin, hasExt, err := user_model.GetExternalLogin(ctx, authSource.ID, gothUser.UserID)
+		if err != nil {
+			ctx.ServerError("GetExternalLogin", err)
+			return
+		}
+		isDisabledByAutoSync := hasExt && extLogin.RefreshToken == ""
+		if isDisabledByAutoSync {
+			opts.IsActive = optional.Some(true)
+		}
 	}
```

### Fix summary

The patch modifies the OAuth sign-in logic to only reactivate users if their deactivation was a result of an automatic OAuth synchronization process (indicated by cleared access tokens). It explicitly avoids reactivating users who were manually disabled by an administrator, ensuring that admin-imposed deactivations are respected.

## GHSA-hrxh-6v49-42gf · google.golang.org/grpc

2026-07-21 · Go · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The gRPC-Go server's control buffer, which handles various control frames (like RST_STREAM, SETTINGS ACKs), did not have a proper throttling mechanism. An attacker could send a large number of specific HTTP/2 frames, causing the control buffer to grow indefinitely and consume excessive memory, leading to a denial of service.

### Impact

An attacker could exhaust the server's memory resources by sending a flood of specially crafted HTTP/2 frames, causing the gRPC server to crash or become unresponsive, thereby denying service to legitimate users.

### Key diff

```
--- a/internal/transport/controlbuf.go
+++ b/internal/transport/controlbuf.go
@@ -96,61 +97,70 @@ func (il *itemList) isEmpty() bool {
 	return il.head == nil
 }
 
-// The following defines various control items which could flow through
-// the control buffer of transport. They represent different aspects of
-// control tasks, e.g., flow control, settings, streaming resetting, etc.
-
-// maxQueuedTransportResponseFrames is the most queued "transport response"
-// frames we will buffer before preventing new reads from occurring on the
-// transport.  These are control frames sent in response to client requests,
-// such as RST_STREAM due to bad headers or settings acks.
-const maxQueuedTransportResponseFrames = 50
+var maxQueuedControlBufferItems = int(envconfig.ControlBufferThrottleLimit)
 
 type cbItem interface {
-	isTransportResponseFrame() bool
+	isThrottled() bool
 }
 
+// throttledItem represents every item in the controlBuffer to which the overall
+// throttling limit applies, other than outgoing HEADERS and DATA frames.
+type throttledItem struct{}
+
+func (throttledItem) isThrottled() bool { return true }
+
 // registerStream is used to register an incoming stream with loopy writer.
 type registerStream struct {
+	throttledItem
 	streamID uint32
 	wq       *writeQuota
 }
 
-func (*registerStream) isTransportResponseFrame() bool { return false }
-
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces a throttling mechanism for the control buffer. It defines a new `isThrottled()` interface for control buffer items and sets a maximum limit (`maxQueuedControlBufferItems`) for throttled items. This prevents an unbounded growth of the control buffer when processing certain types of HTTP/2 frames.

## GHSA-r7wm-3cxj-wff9 · tools.jackson.core:jackson-core

2026-07-21 · Java · **HIGH** 0.0 · Pattern: `DOS→RESOURCE_EXHAUSTION`

### Root cause

The asynchronous JSON parser in Jackson-core did not properly validate the accumulated length of integer numbers against the `StreamReadConstraints.maxNumberLength` limit when processing input in chunks. This allowed an attacker to send a number as a series of single-digit chunks, bypassing the length check that would normally occur for a complete number, leading to an unbounded buffer growth.

### Impact

An attacker could provide a specially crafted JSON input with a very long number, causing the parser to allocate an excessively large buffer. This would lead to a denial of service by exhausting memory resources on the server processing the input.

### Key diff

```
--- a/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/core/json/async/NonBlockingUtf8JsonParserBase.java
+++ b/src/main/java/com/fasterxml/jackson/core/json/async/NonBlockingUtf8JsonParserBase.java
@@ -1325,6 +1325,7 @@ protected JsonToken _startPositiveNumber(int ch) throws IOException
             if (++_inputPtr >= _inputEnd) {
                 _minorState = MINOR_NUMBER_INTEGER_DIGITS;
                 _textBuffer.setCurrentLength(outPtr);
+                _setIntLength(outPtr);
                 return _updateTokenToNA();
             }
             ch = getByteFromBuffer(_inputPtr) & 0xFF;
```

### Fix summary

The patch introduces calls to `_setIntLength(int len)` in the `NonBlockingUtf8JsonParserBase` class at points where the parser yields `_updateTokenToNA()` due to an incomplete number. This ensures that the accumulated integer length is validated against `StreamReadConstraints.maxNumberLength` even when the number is received in multiple chunks, preventing unbounded buffer growth.
